

THE VICTORIAN
INSOLVENT LIST
FROM 1842 TO 1862.




THE VICTORIAN
INSOLVENT LIST,
FROM
1842, TO THE END OF JUNE, 1862,
AND
PUBLIC ASSIGNMENTS,
FROM 1854, TO THE END OF JUNE, 1862,
COMPILED FROM AUTHENTIC SOURCES,
BY
J. NOBLE WILSON.
MELBOURNE :
PRINTED BY EDGAR RAY, COLLINS STREET EAST.
1862. ,


MELBOURNE :
FEINTED BY EDGAE HAY, COLLINS-STEEET EAST.


PREFACE.
I was induced to publish the present compilation because I was told it would be a useful book of reference.
I believe it will. Hitherto when the estate of some insolvent became a subject of enquiry, it has been necessary to make
three distinct searches in the Insolvent Court Records for that information which is here presented at a glance. After the
labor of nearly nine months compiling, arranging, and superintending through the press, I feel that had I fully compre-
hended the task I imposed upon myself it is more than probable that this book would never have been undertaken by
me. Great care has been exercised in compiling the list, and the most scrupulous pains have • been bestowed upon that
portion of it which has reference to the last six or seven years. I trust, therefore, that no material errors will be found
in the book. My motive for undertaking it was to supply a great commercial want, as there is no similar record in
existence. To have verified every entry, it would have been necessary to search through all the records of the Insolvent
Court, —and this would-have involved an expenditure in court fees and in labor, which would have made the book altogether
too costly. 'lt is a reprint of a register which has been kept up day by day for many years past. Wherever any doubt
existed as to the correctness of the register, or wherever there was an apparent discrepancy, the doubt has been cleared
up or the discrepancy rectified by actual search made in the Insolvent Court.
The Appendix contains the list of Insolvents from Ist January, 1862, to the 30th June, 1862, inclusive,
together with a list of such certificates granted, suspended, or refused, and dividends declared, as accumulated during the
progress of this book through the press, but which were too late for insertion in their proper places. The Public Assign-
ments which have occurred within the above period will be found properly arranged.
The following explanations of abbreviations used may be necessary :
Certificates. —Where the date only appears in the column for “ certificates” it means that the certificate was
Granted upon that date. The letter R, or r., signifies that the certificate was Refused. The letter S., or s., indicates
that the certificate was suspended. Where no date is given it will, of course, be taken to mean that no certificate has
issued. Indeed in searching over the court records it is curious to observe what a large proportion of those who file their
schedules fail to apply to the court for a discharge. In some cases I notice that an insolvent will file his schedule, enter
into business, and two or three years afterwards will again become insolvent without ever having obtained a certificate of
discharge from his first insolvency.
Dividends. —ln this column it was my intention to have stated the amount of each dividend declared. The
first page of the book was printed before I altered my plan at the suggestion of one of the Official Assignees. In many
estates several dividends are declared, and these, perhaps, at intervals of a year or more. To state therefore that so much
in the pound was paid, when, perhaps, the amount stated was only a first dividend with one or two more dividends to
follow, would have been to mislead, and was a difficulty which could not be avoided in any other way than by the
method adopted.
Compulsory Sequestrations, are distinguished by the letters c.s. following the name.
J. N. W.
72 Collins-street East, Melbourne, August, 1862.
